Aspects Of Love - Newcastle, UK Tour 06/09/07 Matinee - Master
Matt Rawle, Shona Lindsay, Poppy Tierney, David Essex, Rachel Lynes, Philip Cox, Duncan Patrick, Aoife Nally
*A, with minor bass issues in a couple of places due to sitting front row with a slightly overpowering orchestra. Very limited trade. Wonderful performances from Matt, Shona & Poppy. Rachel was just perfect as Jenny but David sounded drunk and came across as flat in every way - acting, vocals, it's all monotone. David aside, I was absolutely blown away. I'd been worried I might be disappointed having waited so long to finally see a production of this show but I was beyond impressed.*

Aspects Of Love - Newcastle, UK Tour 15/09/07 Matinee - Master
Matt Rawle, Shona Lindsay, Poppy Tierney, David Essex, Rachel Lynes, Philip Cox, Duncan Patrick, Aoife Nally
*A-, not for trade.*

Aspects Of Love - Norwich, UK Tour 28/11/07 Matinee - Master
Matt Rawle, Shona Lindsay, Poppy Tierney, David Essex, Rachel Lynes, Philip Cox, Duncan Patrick, Aoife Nally
*A, not for trade. Dreadful audience. Matt's Alex is an entirely different person to the way he played it in Newcastle. He's gone from making Alex quite sarcastic and unlikable to cute, naive and very smiley. Both ways work for me but I do prefer this quite adorable version. Stranger still - David was great fun and actually won me over. I really liked him... I may need therapy. David & Alex mess up 'She'd Be Far Better Off With You', causing David to adlib at the end.*

*A, not for trade. First performance of the new cast (most of the ensemble plus Greg stepping up to principal Magaldi, with Elena standing in for Yvette for the first Monday only). Elena was clearly having a lot of fun on stage and was actually a little softer with her portrayal than usual. Matt was hilarious, he spent the show with glitter on his face and kept laughing at himself, you can hear him go in HFA & Rainbow Tour especially.... the audience loved him and Elena, and he really fed off it. Greg is a wonderful Magaldi. Funny, adorable, great accent and voice - really shows up how average Gary was in the role.*

Little Shop Of Horrors - London 20/06/07 Evening - Master
Sheridan Smith, Matthew Eames*, Barry James, Alistair McGowan, Jenny Fitzpatrick, Katie Kerr, Millie Mace, Mike McShane
*A, not for trade. Sheridan's voice is a lot better than I thought though she definitely has some weak places and she can't touch Jodie's amazing vocals. She's very funny in the role though sometimes it takes her out of character to get the laugh... I prefer Jodie's more honest take on the character. Though not as good as Paul, Matthew did a great job, he's very nerdy and sweet, and plays it much straighter than Paul does, singing the part without the extreme character voice Paul uses. Loving Millie's new riffs. Very appreciative audience.*

Little Shop Of Horrors - London 30/06/07 Evening - Master

*A, not for trade. Ends after Suddenly Seymour as I had to leave. Best I've seen Paul, though he had the giggles. Everyone was incredibly on (possibly for their first Saturday night in the new theatre? I hate the new theatre.), though I didn't like Sheridan's last part in Suddenly Seymour, it all went a bit flat. The audience loved it anyway.*

Little Shop Of Horrors - Cambridge, UK Tour 11/03/09 - Master
Clare Buckfield, Damian Humbley, Sylvester McCoy, Alex Ferns, Donna Hines, Cathryn Davis, Nadio Di Mambro, Clive Rowe
*A-/B+ - bassy. Not for trade. Finally the Menier production goes on tour, with a few minor changes, and it's still fantastic. The cast are mostly weaker than the London cast but still enoyable. Damian, Cathryn & Clive are fabulous and easily keep the standard up but Clare has obviously studied and copied Sheridan Smith as exactly as she can, though she's too hammy to pull it off well. Alex is visually hilarious but can't sing a note - enjoyable as he is to watch it's quite painful to listen to.*

Martin Guerre - Madrid
Antonio Camacho, Victor Diaz, Carlos Fernández, Eva Rosa Garcia, Virginia Garcia, José Miguel Lacalle, Carlos London, Luis Miguel Lopez, Silvia Lopez, Carmen Porras, David Venancio Muro

Martin Guerre - Watermill Theatre, Newbury 14/07/07 Matinee - Master
Ben Goddard, Kelly OLeary, Andrew Bevis, Jez Unwin, James Traherne, Karen Mann, Johnson Willis, Susannah Van Den Berg, Rosie Timpson, Michael Howcroft, Esther Biddle, Kit Orton
*A, not for trade. Not the audio with skipping that's on a few lists out there, it's a different master. Interesting revised actor musician production from the Watermill (responsible for the Sweeney production that transferred to Broadway). Mostly based around the first incarnation of the show with a few parts spliced in from the later tour and quite a lot that was new. Not sure I'm loving a lot of the changes, especially to the heart of the story, but it worked well for this production. Ben was an incredible Arnaud and worth the ticket alone, Jez made for a great Guillaume and Kelly was fairly average at best as Bertrande - I'd have liked to see something more from her. Andrew did a great job with what he had to work with but the role of Martin was practically written out, and what was left was entirely unsympathetic which was a bit of a waste of him really.*

Martin Guerre - Watermill Theatre, Newbury 11/08/07 Matinee - Master
Ben Goddard, Kelly OLeary, Andrew Bevis, Jez Unwin, James Traherne, Karen Mann, Johnson Willis, Susannah Van Den Berg, Rosie Timpson, Michael Howcroft, Esther Biddle, Kit Orton
*A, not for trade. Really enjoyed this a lot more the second time around, everyone's stepped their performances up even more though I actually find Kelly's thin voice and passive portrayal almost unbearable now. There's something about Andrew's voice I'm kind of in love with and Ben and Jez have somehow managed to get even more fantastic, definitely the standouts of the production.*

Miss Saigon - Melbourne 17/03/07
Laurie Cadevida, Leo Valdez, David Harris, Sophie Katinis, Juan Jackson, RJ Rosales, Christina Tan
*Quiet and suffers from overload, but not bad and perfectly listenable as long as you adjust the volume. I'm not sure I'm liking this production much yet... Laurie is lovely and Leo's incomparable as ever, but David irritates the life out of me and Juan is pretty weak vocally. Everyone else is competant, just not exciting. Odd changes made too, in quite a few songs the orchestrations are completely slowed down, words are changed here and there for no apparent reason, and there's random shouted lines during The Confrontation. 'Where are my manners?' is not what I expect to hear during Room 317... then again I'm very resistant to change.*

The Boys In The Photograph - LIPA 19/04/08 Matinee - Master
Matthew Grace, Jeanna De Waal, Derek Barr, Adam Diggle, Cecilia Ardiles, Rob Gilbert, Terri O'Brien, Richard Loosemore, Bryn Holding, Lauren Martel
*A, not for trade, no exceptions. Workshop/full production of the reworked 'The Beautiful Game' performed by LIPA students in collaboration with Ben Elton & Andrew Lloyd Webber. Gorgeous production with some real standouts in the cast - Jeanna was wonderful in every way, Derek's acting was stunning, and Bryn has fabulous comic timing. Matthew was very good but seemed to have slight vocal trouble early on. As far as the changes go: the best song (Our Kind Of Love) has been cut for no good reason, the new (title) song is gorgeous, most of the changes work wonderfully but the new happy ending just doesn't work for me.*

The Wedding Singer - Ipswich 10/05/08 Matinee - Master
Jonathan Wilkes, Natalie Casey, Jodie Jacobs, Simon Lipkin, Nick Hayes, Stephen Webb, Tricia Deighton, Camille Devine, Carys Gray, Richard Taylor Woods
*B+, not for trade. Never sit in front of a speaker at this show... bass hell for audios. And how do I always manage to sit next to the screamers - even in Ipswich? Not my sort of show but enjoyable anyway... Jonathan was passable, Natalie was sweet but can't lose her accent never mind try an American one, and Jodie was orgasmic - worth the price alone to hear her belt the shit out of the part. And when did Richard Taylor Woods become so magnetic? Average as he was as u/s Chris in Miss Saigon, he stole so many scenes for me in this and he's only featured ensemble.*

Cassidy Janson*, Helen Dallimore, Martin Ball, Suzie Blake, Nigel Planer, Oliver Tompsett*, Caroline Keiff*, James Gillan
*A, not for trade. Cassidy was awesome, a very youthful Elphaba with so much attitude and sarcasm. Her voice was a little rough in places, but generally she still sounded wonderful. Oliver sounded throatier than I remember, he sang the shit out of ALAYM but I still find him more wooden and less charismatic than a plank. I like Caroline so much more than Katie, she actually puts some effort into it.*

Wicked - London 11/06/08 Matinee - Master
Alexia Khadime, Dianne Pilkington, Oliver Tompsett, Andy Mace*, Harriet Thorpe, Caroline Keiff, Jeremy Legat, David Stoller*
*A, not for trade. Really liked Alexia, she's such a breath of fresh air and has an unexpectedly cute childlike quality to her voice. She needs to bring more to her DG but to be fair she's so stunning she could just stand there and be pretty and it'd work. The most original NGD I've seen. I could strangle Dianne because she's actually got the most amazing comic timing and would be so enjoyable if it wasn't for her bizarre voice which is grating on me. Harriet is deliciously evil, but Oliver could be marketed as a cure for insomnia.*

Wicked - London 30/10/08 Matinee - Master
Ashleigh Gray*, Dianne Pilkington, Oliver Tompsett, Desmond Barritt, Harriet Thorpe, Caroline Keiff, Jeremy Legat, Andy Mace
*A, not for trade. Ashleigh has a lovely voice but can't act, she doesn't seem to know what to do with herself and it's all a bit stage school. If you closed your eyes she'd be great, although she screws up INTG quite a bit and the end of NGD a little too. Dianne has grown on me so much and I actually really enjoyed her... And then there's Oliver. Who should be sacked. He gave the most lazy performance I've ever seen, clearly couldn't be bothered to be there and wasn't even remotely in character at any point. It's just horrifying that he's allowed to go on stage like that.*
